de la cure des emorroydes	on the treatment of hemorrhoids:
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the rectum, either one or more, and are old and filled with cold and moist corrupted humors, and are cured as we have said in divisions, but it does not help, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is completely beneath the armpit, little by little in a triangular shape, and one cautery beneath the hip. two times;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you think that his stomach is chilled, and the meat is not cooked, and one sees the face swell up, then on the face put a large cautery on the stomach, as it is before said, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse on all the cautery clave; and let the cautery remain open for a long time. After cure the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thelul, scorch the cautery which looks like a razor, and then put it all ablaze on the cut thelul; and keep your hand so that the cauteries reach the source of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of thelul, cauterize each one as we have said. After curing with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the scrotum, it will provide more relief.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, such an illness comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula appears and it is swollen and exudes pus and corrupted moisture, you should first test it with a small needle, and be careful that you know how deep the fistula is. Then heat the cautery as if it were a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to its size, and repeat the cautery until the corruption is burned, once or twice or thrice, according to its need; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and large vessels. If the fistula goes toward the bladder and the intestines, beware of these places, and do not apply heat to bone, and think that it is insensitive; after cure the area until it is healed, and if the place is swollen and the materials are not removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed. If the material is not removed, know that the place is damaged and the bone at the bottom is rotten; and thus as one of those which we will discuss in their places.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys, and there are strong winds, and it does not take on the taste of a woman, then you should cauterize him on the kidneys on both sides with the key-shaped cautery that we mentioned before; and if we cauterize him in the middle, he will have three cauteries in a line, and they will do more good.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and flabby from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then he should be cauterized on the part above the bladder where the hairs of the pubic hairline begin, one on each side, and each cautery should be as long as a man's fingernail; and he should also have another cautery over the back if it is needed, two if necessary; and the cauteries should be curved as before described.
de la marris	of the bones
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the bones are cold and moist, and cannot conceive, and the flowers (buds?) are corrupted and their terms delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then one should be cauterized around the navel, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and another two cauteries over the back; and the cauteries should be curved, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistors descend to the socket of the hip, and because of this it moves out of its place, and the sign is that the leg is longer than the other when measured together; and one finds the place of dislocation wet, then you must cauterize the dislocation on the socket of the hip with a .i. cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and the cautery should be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make 3 cauteries of olive oil large enough to fit the wound; and let the cautery be as deep as the wound, and heal it until it is better.
de la dolor de la hainche	of hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the hip socket, it is caused by cold and moisture, and the treatment we have described does not help, and the ailment is old: then you must purge the ailment of the gross humors with foul-smelling pills, or other good-smelling pills alike.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, he does cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two methods: namely, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to many methods, among which one is such that you cauterize on the hip socket three triangular cauteries according to this form, and you make a good depth and a large one, and there is between each cautery a space the thickness of a thumb, and the cauteries are olive-shaped; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle over the head of the hip, so that there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier regarding the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains the entire hip, and all the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And it is the manner in which one does sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg. And if it reaches the thigh and leg, then he cauterizes where the pain holds him, three cauteries there where the ailment says that the pain holds him, and one cautery above the ankle of the fourth toes, on the left side a little; and let the cautery be cuticular, and let the thickness of the heart be burned; and if the ailment feels that the pain extends to the big toe or near it, then he is cauterized there where he feels the pain, three points or four at the cautery which is called "points."
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if he feels that the pain is under the knee toward the thigh, use a scalpel or circular cautery, and be careful with all your cauteries not to leave the cautery in place so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I have seen many who had cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so long that the leg was entirely swollen, and the foot as well, and it was pierced and corrupted all through the foot. Afterwards he died from a bellyache.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, do cautery on one and the other according to this method. // And they said about the cautery of the hip, of which here is the method: make 1 such iron and let it be as thick at the head as a little finger, or a bit less, and let it be pierced with holes and spaces between them the distance of a finger's width; and let there be 2 projections on each side, and let them be like knots, and have 1 handle of well-made iron; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and dripping, and then put it on the bone of the hip that is ill, and turn it onto the healthy side; and cauterize once with 1 cautery and leave it for 3 days; and then make a poultice from butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the application of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Bukhari says that we use this cautery sparingly because of its frightening appearance, and seldom see those who use it; nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured by anyone in whom it is used.
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes in the back, whether from sitting or from impact or from excessive discharge, or from similar appearances of expanded cold matter, none of these indications are suitable for cauterization except for that which comes from the diffusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after the patient has voided foul pills or other similar substances, to apply a cautery on the back, where the pain persists, in three lines marked with ink, and in each line .v. cauteries or more depending on the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be performed according to the cautery which is called "pin"; and if you see fit, perform .iij. cauteries or .iiij. with the cautery key tool according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a stiff neck when they wake up, and fear; and you will find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you cure it, then cauterize it with the cautery of salt according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery purples each part of the spine evenly. And if you see it, cauterize around the spine with a cautery point .ij. lines or .iij., and let the points be close to each other. After curing the site until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware of administering cautery in gangliness which is in spasm of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	There are two types of cautery: one is by fire and the other is by salt. The salt cautery is better; it does not burn the flesh or the bone or the nerve, but is a great remedy for pains that come from the head.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain in the joints is caused by moisture that has spread throughout the body's limbs, and when the pain is in the feet, which they properly call "podagra", and when it is caused by a cold and cannot be cured by medicine, then it is cured by cautery in the following way: make the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is a need for you to apply cautery on the side of the foot, make a small dot with cautery. And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make cautery marks on each knee, 3 or 4 cauteries in each place, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand against it for longer than until the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, administer cautery as we have said in that chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make marks around the wrist for 2 lines; and if there is no more pain in the arms, make marks on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and give medicine. For if you take good care of him and cleanse his blood, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root of the syphilis
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rot occurs in the armpit and the bowels descend into the groin, as is often the case with new injuries, one should not eat on the day of treatment. Instead, one should consume food that loosens the belly so that the feces will exit the body; then, make the patient sit up with his back against your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are relieved and return to their proper position. Take the fire cautery and brand its shape onto the skin above the armpit joint on the bone of the arm, marking a sign that resembles half of a circle on the upper body; then heat up the cautery instrument:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and dripping with pus. Then reset the bowels to their proper position; and the minister should hold his hand over the patient so they do not return to their previous state; and treat the thighs of the patient, and place a pillow under his thighs, and another servant on top of the thighs, and yet another on the buttocks, holding his hands down. Then apply the cautery onto the sign all along your hand, keeping it straight and firm until you reach the bone. If you do not reach the bone the first time, repeat the process again until you reach the bone; be very careful that the bowels do not protrude when applying the cautery, so as not to burn the patient, or cause other harm, or even death.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you should know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts will be in vain. The cautery for children should be delicate according to their size, and the same for adults, proportional to their size; after three days, treat the area around the cautery with butter until the burn is healed; then treat it with other ointments until it is fully healed, and have the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound can close properly; and one should be careful not to move too much, so that the bowels do not protrude when moving around.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, let him be given a well-made bandage, and wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and guards against too great fullness of drinking and eating, and from talking too much; and when he does this instruction, he will be completely healed. And I will say hereafter about the cure of cutting in his scrotum.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture in the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they are not growing anymore, do to him .1 cautery of the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let it burn the third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that one should cauterize with a cautery with 3 angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but first sign the location of the anus and make a line along the width above the rupture, and another from below, and hold your hand in between throughout the cautery. But the first cauteries are lighter and easier.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any limb, from falling or injury, and the pain persists for a long time, and medicine does not help, then cauterization is needed with a cautery called 'needle', and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, and its tortuosity and pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, that's good; if not, do another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom: one must change the cautery on the limb that is nearest to it, so you should continue with the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of miasma
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Miasmas are sometimes cleared with a cautery for great aid, and so are diseases that come from putrefaction of blood and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is in its early stages, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and neither subsides nor remains, and you doubt that corruption might spread throughout the body, then do 5 cauteries on the head: 1 in the middle of the head, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hairline; and 2 on the temples, and 1 behind on the nape of the neck; and let your hand be so that the cautery reaches the bone, and as long as the skin comes out so that the vapors of the gross humors can come out; and cauterize on the mole according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the ulcer is scattered everywhere; and it is clearly losing ground, then you should cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned: one cautery on the head, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, five cauteries on the spine of the back, one large cautery on the croup and another smaller one, two cauteries on the two shoulders; two cauteries on the elbows, two cauteries on the tendons of the feet, one cautery on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the back of the calf, so that you do not burn them. Sometimes a cautery is made on the bone of the finger, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And you should know that the more cauteries you do, the more help it will bring, and the patient will feel no pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already rotted away. And the cauteries should be large or small according to the limbs and joints, depending on what you find in the ways of the irons. After that, treat the wound with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	of inflammation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling occurs in a limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, but does not heal, then cauterize the limb according to its size; make the cautery somewhat deep in the thickness of the skin. Then treat with ointments until it heals. Sometimes cauterization is done on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit point of a nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of alder trees
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" occurs, and medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a somewhat deep cautery according to the thickness of the skin, so that the whiteness is removed and its color changes; then treat with a poultice made from equal parts of flax seed, lentils, rosemary oil, and a mixture of colon blood and almond blood; bind it with a cloth and keep it in place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of sores by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre comes at the beginning and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And yet wise men say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen more than once; and it is a more certain thing to be cauterized around the edge, using a cautery called "circle," as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot subside
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called  "adubelati," and it is slow to heal, either due to the excess fluid it produces or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, very old) and have little blood, or due to the season; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; after that, leave it as it is. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through, then heat the cautery tool from which comes the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand over the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" as long as the cautery has pierced the skin, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it throughout in such a way that the course of the pustule is relieved. After the healing is complete, then cure it.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of disease is called  "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a melting of the flesh, for it melts the limbs just as fire dries up withered lines. If you see this disease in a place that can withstand cautery, then heat the cauteries very small and large, depending on what is suitable for the affected area; then cauterize all over until you reach all the way to the corruption, removing all of it so that nothing corrupted remains. Then leave it for 3 days and apply a poultice made with oil onto the cauterized areas until the fire burns are healed and all the corruption is gone. After 3 days, if new flesh has grown, that is good; but if not, then repeat the cautery on the affected areas. This melting disease can sometimes be cured by medication instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is generally more effective. I have already described the cure for medication in the section on "Medicine for Ulcers": refer to it when needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of sores that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that in the feet by default a disease called "clos" according to our intention arises, and is a large faulty tumor that blisters the foot. And the cautery for this disease is according to two methods: fire cautery, and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is that you heat one cautery as much as a feather, as it is a pen of a quill, and it is made of good iron to the measure that it can touch the claw from all sides, and it has thin edges; after that, put it all hot on the claw, and turn your hand all around the claw until it reaches the bottom of the claw; and let it be thus for three days until it begins to exude pus; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with salt, and leave the poultice all night, and the claw will fall off and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment impregnating charcoal until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by default throughout the body, and many times in the hands and feet, then you should administer hot water cautery; and it is in such a way: take a rod of copper or iron, or a quill pen, and put it on the claw and the wart, that is to say, warts; and place the rod so that it porridges all around, then put a little bowl of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the claw, and can find the hot water a deep path to the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted at all its roots. So do one after another, until you extract all those who are in the body, then cure them with ointments that generate charcoal.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever, or any other cause, you should make four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebrae; and one cautery on the foot, and one over the stomach with the olive-wood cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes they appear as sore pustules or stinking pustules due to putrid matter. You should cauterize them at the beginning with a thin stick of myrtle that has been heated, or with a long piece of aristolochia, or with a lentil-shaped cautery. Sometimes they are cauterized as soon as they appear, according to this method; thus the superfluous matter from which they come is disrupted and destroyed, and they are healed. But this should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great flows of blood occur from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to light, or at the incision of an abscess, or on the cautery of the limb, and in similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, you must quickly put your finger on the wound of the vein and hold it very tightly until the blood is staunched beneath your finger and no drop flows out; then take several small and large olive-wood cauteries and heat them until they are all red; then take either a large or small piece of wool according to the size of the wound and the location where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds again when you lift your finger from the wound and the cauteries are extinguished, quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until the bleeding is staunched; and be careful not to hurt the nerve that is nearby, and no other harm should come to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be staunched well by itself if the artery is large, except by one of four methods that we have mentioned: by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by a strong ligature with thread, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stanch blood; and it should be bound and pressed firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers a tight bandage or places burning objects on top, or similar things, will not benefit if only a little.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and there is no mirror or medicine available, then one should put their index finger on the wound as we have said, and tightly apply pressure above the wound and vein; and they should not move it but moisten it with cold water frequently so that the blood becomes cold and congealed and tightly applied; and make inquiries in advance about what is needed for cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases that require cauterization with fire or burning medicine, and the causes and the instruments and the forms of cauterizations; and I will go through this chapter by the same path so that one may more easily find what they desire.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is fitting, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to attempt this foolishly. For many types of people come for treatment: some are so desperate because of their illness that they quickly change due to the novelty of their condition, and because of the seriousness of their illness; and one must fear such people.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these there are those who give you their trust and say: "Wait, I am healed"; but the disease is stubborn. You should not listen to such people foolishly, but place more confidence in your honor than in your desire, and do not act rashly but wisely from what you know for certain, and from what you can earn and gain; and use prognostication and indication in treating illnesses where salvation is directed; and this will help you achieve a good reputation, glory, and a legacy of praise.Car il n’est rien si granz que li homes ne fassent en cest monde de la medicine, qui soit tant grant chose que la medicine elle mesme. Car il a beausseins et bontés si grans qu’il est miracle de les conaistre; et ne doit on mie de cela merveilleer, car nature est miracleuse.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have outlined this chapter for you in discussing chapter chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cautery, which I have discussed from the head down to the feet, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Do you know that this disease often comes to children when they are born, and when the birth canal is too narrow for the child; and sometimes it comes from other reasons unknown to us.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those I have seen, death was swift; therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave the treatment in several parts.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I saw a child whose head was swollen with fluid, and the swelling increased every day until he could no longer support it; he died from the pressure of the fluid which had accumulated under the bone between the brain and skull, between the brain and bone. If the fluid is located there between the brain and bone, and if the abscess is small, split the head with a wide incision as long as two fingers so that the fluid can flow out; and here is how you should treat hydrocephalus:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the fluid is deeper and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the fluid is under the bone, and you see the creases of the head opening in each part, and the fluid leaks out when you press it with your hand from within, and this has not helped: then you should split the head into four parts according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all moisture with force. After that, open up the folds of cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound by tenting and poultices, and let the head be bound tightly, and give the patient dry meat to eat, as much as will remove moisture from the member until it is healed and comfortable.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to make an incision is to observe where the abscess is largest and the gathering of pus is most concentrated; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut where the abscess is open and the pus gathers, and cut according to what you are able; and be careful not to cut the artery, or blood will flow and the patient will die from blood loss and moisture evacuation.
de reume	from gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When someone suffers from a condition called "cataract" in the eyes or elsewhere, and the disease is old, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last resort is cautery with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them open, the patient should face away from you; then rub the area around the eyes with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then squeeze the patient's neck with all your might using a .1.-inch-wide bandage; then look where the vein bleeds, and the points are after the ears, and they are very close to each other; then sign the points inside, then cut both of them with an acute spatula about two parts deep so that the vein reaches the bone, and this should be done from the side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see that, put the spatula under the artery and cut it from above, cutting through as well about two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, let the blood flow continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, then you must measure the amount of space of three digits, then cut down and slit to the bone; and the amount of blood to be let out is six ounces, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery; then examine the wound: if it remains over the bone without any pus, so that no hot abscess comes, then extract the wound and ligate, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of the emetic
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient vomiting comes, and a sharp catarrh, due to moisture from the tears and heat in the temples and ancient madness and similar things, and he is treated by various methods of medicine and all that does not help him, then we should open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extraction is that the patient pulls back his hair from his temples, and feels the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and is little relaxed by pressure in some men who are too cold; and if it is relaxed, he stretches his neck with some cloth, then rubs the area with some rough cloth, and washes the area with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatulum of which there is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with tweezers, and separate it well from the tissues underneath in each part; and if the artery is thin, return it to the tip of the fingernail, then cover that part according to the quantity of the two bones. For if it is not covered, the blood will not stop flowing everywhere.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the 16th part up to the 3rd; and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound heals, and bleeding comes gradually; then cover the excess between the two ties in the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with an iron cautery up to the bone until the bones are cut; and this is the main treatment if the patient does not have a fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization helps to dry up moistures, therefore it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts it on top of well-made tents; and when they are removed, it is cured with dry medicines that cause the formation of scar tissue, and with tenting, until it is healed; and if there is a break in the artery during as much as you work on it, then hurry to cover it by cauterization, or you employ vitriol and hold it in your hand so that the blood is stanched; and if you don't have that at hand, then put your finger over the spot so that the blood congeals, and moisten the spot with cold water until the bleeding stops, and then bind it as tightly as it should be; and what is better and lighter for the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of 16 parts, but the cutter must be quite thick so that its heat lasts longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the strumenti is too thin, it holds its heat less well.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And you should have between the two knives a thickness of one digit, and then when you have made the incision in both places, place the hot iron on until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and the two heads should be separated because they are not soldered together by this cautery from top to bottom; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears are flowing from the eyes that are on top of the forehead, and there is no benefit from medicine that is applied, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel pulse movement as if from trembling; and when the eyelids are thin and moist so that the eyelashes have fallen off, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancients called it "cure contused", and you should treat a patient with this condition by shaving the hair from their forehead, then making .iii. incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; let one of the incisions be as wide as two fingers, running straight down through the middle of the forehead to the bridge of the nose, and the other two at either side, above the eyebrows, taking care not to cut into the arteries which are located at either side, above the eyebrows; keep your hand away from the jawbone, and let each incision be as wide as three fingers across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have ready a piece of sponge and clean cloth to wipe away the blood, then apply the plaster of pitch and wax, mixed in equal parts, while it is still warm:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision at the temple to the second incision; and scorch all of the skin between the .ii. incisions to the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second incision, then remove this plaster.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision the instrument called "culter", which is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other, and it is shaped thus:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the incision towards the chest and the armpit, and the lower part towards the bone, and bind it tightly until it reaches the middle split. And tie up all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, so that the incision is continuous until it reaches the opening of the chest, and then make another incision in the middle split until the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and express the area for the extracted blood; then put a tent made of old cotton in each split, and place moistened cloths in wine, oil, and garlic on top, and guard against hot abscesses coming to it; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and administer a large amount of warm water, and then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has a constant and habitual catarrh, and you see that the eyes are pale and sunken, and the vision is weakened, and there is pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then you may know from these signs that those matters and this catarrh do not come from one vein only, but from many veins, and that it comes from the brain, and its cure lies therein.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you should command the patient to lean back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one on top. i. poc. And start from the left temple incision to the right temple, and cut up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that move when eating; and once the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then insert old cotton between the two lips of the incision and cover it with linen bandages; then apply wet cloths soaked in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is healed, you should rub the bone until new flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same way: take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice out of it; and administer it to these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the treatment of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, or animals, or stones, or similar objects such as iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas; or flowing substances such as water and garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear, whether a stone or something else that does not adhere to the ear nor grow in it, then expose the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, then drop some oil of violets or oil of sisamen onto it, and then perform an extraction; and have the patient sneeze with a nostrum, plug the nostrils when sneezing occurs, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and keep the ear elevated. Often this treatment will work; and if not, then perform an extraction using fine tweezers, for which see the following form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it pops out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, then perform an extraction using a small, thin needle of soft metal; and if it does not pop out in this way, make a brass hook and insert its tip firmly into the ear canal, and plug the area around the hook with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the hook; then pull outward firmly, for often it will come out in this way as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take some glue and attach a bird to it, and place some instrument designed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull outward.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all these things that we have said, then be quick to split the ear so that an abscess forms there, and a spasm; and the manner of splitting is that you first make the patient fast for three days, and draw blood according to his condition, then have him sit between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small slit in the root of the ear at the fat where it depends; and the slit should be shaped like a moon, so that you reach the stone, then extract it according to your ability, and suck it strongly with your mouth; and treat it until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is in and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer .i. spatule, held subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then pull it out with subtle tweezers and with a sucking instrument, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the acute case that the earache goes to the ears, the patient should use the first remedy, and open the ear with old cotton. And let him lie on his back with the affected ear upwards. If the earache jumps out through the air, that's good. If not, take several small stones according to the size of your finger, heat them in the fire; then put one end of the stone into the ear, and press the other end with your finger, and make a fire with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to do this from stone to stone until all the ache is driven out, as we have said in the case of the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is a small body like a flea or similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is a large body that one can feel, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section and tract on distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must examine the ear in the sun; if any worms appear, then pull them out with fine tweezers, and if none appear, then take the quill of a goose feather and pierce the eardrum.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.
