Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	It is narrow underneath and wide above. And push in the thinnest end of the quill into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient; then suck firmly on the quill; do this repeatedly until all the worms come out. And if they do not come out, then stop up the quill with cotton as I have said regarding stones; and if they do not emerge as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tried in the extraction of worms, and you will find them in the section on distillations; and distill your oils and remedies into the ear through this instrument, so that the quill is the source of the remedy as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is made of silver or brass with a small hole underneath and holes above for distilling; and to press the distillate into the instrument with a well-made brass instrument for this purpose, and if you wish, take a razor and wrap cotton around the blade; then pour your oil or juice and any remedies you wish into the quill, and the quill is in the ear; then place the razor over the cotton and press your hand gently so that the remedy is distilled onto the eardrum; and the patient feels it inside, and the distillation is a little warm from the fire so that it is not too cold when it enters the ear; and guard against it being too hot, for the remedy would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear stoppers
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an opening in their ears; and the same thing happens to men due to a wound or a growth within the ear, and sometimes this stopper occurs deep within the ear, so it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is only a slight displacement of the opening, which can be easily seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it occurs deep within the ear and cannot be seen, it is a difficult condition in many ways, and in such cases, one should hold the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane visible, then observe how the stopper forms.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointed at the front and back, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the membrane is due to a growth or the body of the ear, then grip it with тонé pins, and gently peel it away until all the growth is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the growth is embedded in the ear, take a fine, light razor, heat it slightly in the fire, and apply it to the body of the ear. If you feel the growth, which causes great pain to the patient when he hears, pierce gently, and be careful not to cut the nerves of the ear; then insert a tent into the ear according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed; then take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder over powdered vitriol; and if you see any swelling in the ear, you should draw out the tent and replace it with another tent moistened with cerate made from olive oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and apply it to the ear; and use other treatments that stop the bleeding from the distilling veins.
de la char des papieres	of paper charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This poultice comes from plants when they are moist and dry; you should spread it with tweezers and tongs, and the root of a spathe; then put powdered vitriol on top.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if there is no scurf, cauterize it with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision heals; and many times they return, until nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come as poultices from plants that look like hail in their shape and hardness, and this disease is therefore called 'hail', and it is an assembly of thick moisture in the paper above and below; its work is such: take care if the hailstone breaks from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know; then open it with tweezers, and peel it. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, it will not harm the patient; and if the split is large, they put in a stitch, and heal it until it is clean; and if it is small, they do not force it, for the ointment will restore and heal it at once.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then invert the paper, and grasp the hailstone with tweezers and squeeze from both sides; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hailstone is crushed, wash the eye with salted water, and clean the area of any pus until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat around the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is woven into the membranes above the paper, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it affects their eyes greatly; and they have cataracts in the mornings, and cannot look at sunlight because the tears rush to their eyes. And so they lie on their faces again and sleep with their eyelids closed, and the moisture and appearance of the eye cover the exinach, which becomes visible through the eye. And when you press on the area with your fingers, the exinach comes out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the treatment is that the patient places his head on your lap; then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach in each part, and then place it over the eye; and press with your fingers from both sides so that the exinach gathers within the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moist area with a spatulum, making the incision no larger than the wound made for vein opening; and in various cases, the exinach comes out through the incision, depending on its shape like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	So take a piece of cloth and hold it between your fingers and thumb, and move your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to touch the fissure, or you will reach all the way to the eye and blister it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrescence opens at the beginning of the fissure, gently widen the fissure slightly so that it appears; then pull as we have said, and moisten clothes in vinegar and water, and place them on the area, and apply bandages tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who grind and put something on to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then treat it until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes in that place, then treat it with cooling poultices until it is healed.Et si li maux est de la chair qui est mortifiee par cause de l’huile ou par cause d’autrui mal, si covient le faire saigner, et mettre sus emplaustre assouajant; puis la faire boire vin chaud, et donner l’alume, et garder que li sang ne soit trop fort.
des poilz des papieres	of the hair of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers, uneven and different from their natural state, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases, such as tears, softening of the papers, and white film, leading to destruction of the eyes; there are four ways to treat this: through cauterization with fire, or with a medicine applied directly to the eye, or through incision and stitching, or with canes, depending on what I will describe.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's eye in your dominant hand, then turn the eyelid to the left; if it returns to its original position, that is good; otherwise, insert a needle and thread through the eyelid, close to the edge of the discolored area where the uneven hairs are growing, and run the thread over the entire eyelid. Then, with a scalpel, make an incision under the eyelid, along the uneven hairs, from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove the thread and place a small piece of cotton and cloth under the eyelid. Mark a figure eight on the eyelid, like the shape of a myrrh roll, but the shape should correspond to the amount you see the eyelid raising or distorting.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a need to cut out a large portion of the eyelid, do so according to how much the eyelid has softened; then make an incision along the two lines you marked, starting from the large tear duct and ending at the small one. Make one cut close to the natural hairs in the shape of a root, then insert the needle into one of the corners of the wound, and pull it through; then remove the skin entirely. Bring the two edges of the wound together with a single thread and a fine needle, and absorb any blood, then use something sticky to tighten the excess thread above the two eyebrows; if not, don't worry about it. Leave the stitch and threads in place for three or four days, then remove them and treat the wound with dry, compressing remedies without stitches. The eyelid will heal on its own (as the ancients say), and this is a safe procedure.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure that is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have told, at 3 inches apart according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut out those on top with small scissors evenly according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you don't have the strength to hold the tweezers, and it is not even, then take a needle with which he has .1. string, and pierce through the figure; and pierce another string through the large artery, and the second string through the small one, and bring together between your fingers the strings evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above which you have marked, as we have told, then bring together the 2 lips of the wound by suturing, and heal it until it is cured; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerot
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes the hair of the paper is turned around: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suturing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of warts is as follows: you must first turn the paper and place it inside according to what I have said, then make two warts using art, and two thin lines as long and wide as the spatumile; then tie two knots at both ends where you hold the threads; then bring one knot close to the other gently above the paper on the eye, and pull the two warts from their roots; leave them like that for a few days, and the skin that was pulled will die and harden and fall off as it shrinks.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time and the skin is pulled too tightly, then treat it until it heals; and when the wound has healed and the paper has fallen off, the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two warts that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the tools are such that you thread a thin needle with a fine silk thread, then tie the ends together gently and make the length of the threads about a palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread in the spatumile, and tie the end of this thread as well; then put the patient's head in your lap, and let them face the sun so that their skin is exposed, for it is a delicate treatment; then thread the needle all the way into the root of the hair close to the skin until you draw it out through the paper with the natural hair; then pull the hair all the way up to the spatumile, and insert the hair into the spatumile along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hunt is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you will treat the hunt underneath to the very end that you have ordered, until the hunt comes out of the hole above and you see it through the vision of the eye; then you will treat the hunt and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, accompany it with a long hair from the horses' mane, and let it grow with that which you leave, until it is elongated and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eyelash
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or the eyelash comes, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It happens suddenly from an injury, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the natural way is when the eyelash comes out through the wound in the eye, or from cutting or cautery, and one should treat it so that it does not break. And the method of treatment is that you split the wound, loosen its edges, and put in there tents of linen, and ligature it until it is healed; and one must not use in its treatment things that dry and restrict. For if you do that, the disease will become worse than before; but work with moisturising things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or vinegar and seed of linseed are cooked, and ointments of diaquilon melted in some oils, and wrap it up with a tent, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the goal of your treatment is to ensure that it does not fuse according to the shape it was before; and these works that we have spoken of are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the shape it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease, which is truly called "axacrati", has both natural and accidental causes. The accident comes from wounds, incisions, cautery, and similar things; and the way to treat it is as follows: you take a needle with a double thread, pierce the flesh at the outer corner of the left eye so that the thread passes through to the right side, making sure the thread lies above the needle. Then the flesh above the needle is pressed down, and the cut is made wide enough for a spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the slit, turn the paper, and make 2 slits along the sides inside the paper; the ends of the 2 slits on each side of the incision you have made should form angles so that when they are brought together, the shape is like the shape of the letter "J". Then remove the paper, according to the quantity that its edges are cut under, from what follows the paper; then bring the two severed parts together and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said with softening medicines, and with bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a split or a stitch or cautery, then one must make a clean split underneath the hairs of the paper, and according to what is stated above; then unravel between the two lips of a tent, as I have said; and one should perform the operation according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares remedies with all his might, so that the figure returns to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suddenness happens to human beings in such a way that the paper above is separated from the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then one must therefore push the tip of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and hold it with tweezers, so as to grasp what is cut in the subtle spatula, which is neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient does not feel that the spatula is too sharp or cutting into the eye; and make your incision, by which you peel away this membrane, very lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and when all of this membrane has been removed, there may sometimes be a sore in the eye, and it should be washed with warm water and then with cool water, and then a tent of linen should be placed between the paper and the eye, and lamb's wool dampened in egg white should be laid over the eye; and after the third day, one should use collyrium and soothing remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that there are two types of ulcer: one is nervous and resembles a hard ulcer, and the other is not nervous but resembles white congealed moisture; when touched with iron and pinched, it feels like paneling to the fingernails, but no one can feel it. Both types begin at the outer corner of the eye, growing little by little until they cover the entire eye, obscure its light, and impair its movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is to have the patient place his head against your hand, then work the eyelids; and hold the paper in your hand, then pinch the edge of the ulcer with tiny pincers and stretch it upward; next take a needle and thread a horsehair, or cow's hair, or ox's hair through it, and double over the point of the needle slightly before inserting it into the ulcer, and tie the ulcer with a thread and stretch it upward, then scrape along the edge of the ulcer from its base toward the eyebrow until you reach the tear gland, using tiny movements and leaving the natural flesh of the tear gland untouched, so that the incision does not affect the flow of tears; sometimes only the edge of the ulcer needs to be tied, as we have said, with thread, then scrape along the spatumile:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatumile does not touch the fleshy membrane and rupture it, and that the tear gland is not pierced; after the incision, drop a little powdered chalk into the eye, and make a collar out of litarge, leaving it in place until the next day; then treat the eye as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push in the needle, and the hook cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured by medicines; and they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the eye of the malady, and take the spatule lightly poked according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail gently, and if you see that it is not lessened and the reason is pressing, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litarge and red copper ore, ground together, and stop the eye until the next day; then start the other work according to this same method, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is nothing contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then start the work again as before, until it is healed.Si li ungle est ost, adonques tu le remets, et si li est alongie, adonques tu le rompts; car il ne poait demorer a son leu.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the arm hurts the eye greatly through great harm, then suspend it at the elbow, and cut off a part and not all, so that the body of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In the eyes of some men sometimes grows red flesh, and covers the pupil and turns upwards, and resembles a rose of marble; and the action is that the patient puts his head in yours, then he works on the eye, and pulls all that flesh to the hinges suitable for this, and holds it firmly; then cut the first flesh, and go cutting little by little to the end, and be careful not to bleed the eye during the operation; and the incision of the spatumile which we have described in the incision of the nail, and with small forces from which one removes the pus, just as the form after this chapter demonstrates it;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply to the eye oil of seal, or you can distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the eye a cotton bandage with egg white so that it is secured from hot abscess; and if there is nothing left, and the pain increases, and you doubt hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things for hot abscess; then return to your operation until it is healed, and thus do when the flesh is grown in the eye through this likeness.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless you should ease the treatment of every weak part of the natural way; and in accidental work with iron, do not put your hand into any of those works until you see that this member can bear such work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of them
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Such are red veins which are covered above the eye, and tolerate their work and weaken the eye all day. Therefore, first, you must look at the eye, in which such is, is outside, and there is no other disease except the evil; then he should be treated in this way: instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, then gently compress those veins all around according to his wisdom, and let the compresses be double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two compresses be in degrees in .i. body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then you can squeeze these veins gently, and let the blood flow out an hour after another, until you see the veins recede from the eye; and be careful not to cut the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not slip outside these veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the eye green and red color to corrupt what is left of the scabies.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to squeeze all of this in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye of soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for a few days until the pain is relieved and there is a hot abscess, then begin again according to what is written above until he is healed; and this is the way of doing it:
de la fistule de l’oil	of eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Examine the fistula, which is called "arissati" in Latin: when you cure it with cautery and medicine that burns according to what I have written before, and it is not healed, then there is a wound in it where you should cut into the abscess, the place where it should be, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, you will see the decay and blackness; there is the instrument of which this is the form; it is called "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron into a flat head, and punctured like a file as it is in its current form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the location of the decayed bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little so that you know the decay has been removed; do this several times, then restore the site with astringent medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the site is sewn up and a boil grows there, and the body of the bow is sewn up and remains that way for 40 days, and it does not heal and no bad accident occurs, you can know that it is healed; if not, then do nothing but draw out the fistula through the hole in the bone according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with watery medicines, and when it is uncovered take a needle according to this form, and let the head of the needle be flat on three sides, and the shaft tapered to a point as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone under the ulcer, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the needle around until it pierces the bone and he feels the pain due to the wound from his hand; then restore the site with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the boil grows and hardens the site, go to the nail; this is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open fully and there is no disturbance to the eye or diminution, then you must ligate the patient; then cleanse the eye, then place leeches or a cupping glass without piercing to draw out any fluid; then apply an ointment made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla over the eye, and then compress it with bandages and cloth. The manner of the bandages is that you take soft cloth, double each one over four times, and then place one over another according to the quantity that the eye requires; then compress it firmly from above with a hard bandage, and repeat the leeches to draw without piercing; then remove the leeches and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the ligature becomes soft, you must compress it tightly; then remove the ligature after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then repeat the ointment and the bandages and the ligature and the leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from a torn woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in woven fabric, then it opens and appears like a grain of resin, and is terrible to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you pierce an needle in the root of the part below up to the part above; and then pierce another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the armhole; and tie the fabric around the eye, and compress it well, then remove the needle and place a soft egg-soaked cloth over the eye; and leave it until the threads tear with the fabric, then cleanse the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is constrained by the fabric in a circle of cloth all around, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great indication, then pierce them with a sharp spatulate instrument which enters through the eye socket, and scrape away the white moisture and bring the eyes down, and enter inside immediately; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease, which is called "alkunati", is nothing but water accumulated in the eye socket, resembling a descent of water, but it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the operation is that you make the patient sit on a raised seat or chair, then hold the head between your hands, tilting it so that you see the water come out from under the eyelids. Then it should be wiped away, and the light shone into the eye to check the patient can see as before; if not, know it is water, and if the discharge from the eye socket does not appear as described, then tilt the patient's head again and use a sharp spatulate instrument to press on the conjunctiva next to the cornea and the cornea itself until the water comes out. Then instil into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek boiled with honey; then it should be treated with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearance of the diseases in the division, and what should be done to pierce it; then act according to health. You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light so as not to see the sun, and close his healthy eye and squeeze it tightly; then place the paper over the eye if the eyes are on the left, or on the right hand if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called 'almagda', or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the thickness of a hair in that white part of the eye to the part where the tear duct is, then gently insert the instrument called 'almagda' and turn your hand so that it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that the almgada reaches the empty space; and the measure of the path of the almgada should be at the bottom of the measurement of the space between the pupil and the edge of the iris; this is the crown of the eye; you will then see the bone in this paper through the clarity of the horny tissue, then place the instrument where the ailment is, then express it from under one path after another. If the fluid flows out now, the patient will see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, if the fluid rises up the second path, insert the instrument and when it is stuck in and not rising, gently pull out the almgada by turning your hand a little; then put in the eye a little seal gem, and take it out of this eye. Then place on top of the eye a compress of linen soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg white, and bind it with the healthy eye. We and those of our time put on a mixture of comfrey with plenty of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almgada cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then you must use the instrument called 'albarit', which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too deeply, but make a small incision, then fill it with alum, as we have said; and when the work is finished, prepare for the patient a dark room in which he can sleep on his back in a dark place; and let him be free of all movement, and eat light foods, and do not move his head or to the right or left, and let him be tied according to his condition for three days; then untie him in that same dark room, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day; and you should not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should lighten this, so that the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And if there are hot abscesses, you should untie the eye before the seventh day, and use a remedy for abscesses; and when it is soothed, untie the vision and put on an eyepatch to cover one eye, and let him stay in that dark room. And then go out of the house a little and return to his condition; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iran, who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, and suck out the water, but I have never seen anyone doing this in our land, nor have I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagest, because those who do not know them will see them; and they are properly made of bronze.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the heads be of the same subtle metal, and the rear in 3 angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	of the eye above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes there are various nosebleeds, from which some seem like scorpions with many feet; and if there are any with a dark blue color, and some with a light blue color. For this type of nosebleed that is light blue and not dark, you should have the patient lean back against the sun; open their nostrils, and pour the liquid onto those nosebleeds, and pull them outwards; then cover what you can sustain with the spatumile's subtle tip from one side, as long as you know that the nosebleed has stopped.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains which one cannot cover, then open it at its thinnest and lightest part, so that nothing remains; and if without swelling, or an abscess forms, then lancing as appropriate; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten to cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the evil is removed, then apply ice or cold water and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the ears are affected and moisture reaches to the palate, you know it is cured; and if the moisture does not drain as it should, you know there is purulent matter in the bone above, because the instrument did not cut through: then you must insert a large piece of linen thread, knotted at one end, with the knot at the tip of the nose, leaving a space of a digit or less between each knot; and let the patient hold the thread in his mouth by its tail to the limit of his strength, and draw it up the nostril until it reaches the palate; many children do this in school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it. Then hold one end of the thread in one hand, and the other end which comes out through the mouth in the other hand, and move them gently from side to side while feeling along the thread with your fingers. Do this until you feel that the thread has corroded and removed all the corrupted matter; then draw out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, then reinsert it into the nostril as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded and removed all that remains of the corruption. Then insert a plug of cotton wool into the nostril for several days while it heals; if medicine is needed to dry out the passage, use it. This is the instrument used to cleanse the nose, through which oils and medicines are instilled.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and it must also be straight; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be filled for cleansing the nose; and there should be a handle on the instrument to hold it while heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the nose and grows and becomes large, to such an extent that it is visible to the eye; therefore one should cut it at the beginning and remove the whole pustule, then place on the fire cautery or burning medicine; but if one delays cutting it until it has become large, take care whether it is hard, discolored in color, and of poor sensation: then do not touch it with iron, for it is an encrusted abscess; because when it is cut once, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due to pressure rather than discoloration, and you see that one can cover it all, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose has been cut and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these cartilage channels, it benefits few men. Therefore, whenever this happens to anyone, you should examine whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then cut off the .ij. lips at one stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are torn on both sides, you should scrape away all the parts of their skin until they heal, then sew together the .ij. lips at one stitch, press them together, and powder with powdered dragon's blood, and powdered incense; and place a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster on top of the powders, and leave it until it dries by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the abdomen; or with thread, as I have already informed you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hollows of the lips there are hard abscesses, similar to grains of wheat, small and large; therefore you must split the lips, and cut into each pustule with pincers, and scrape away the pus from every part; then apply powdered vitriol to the incision, until the blood is dried up; then use raw garlic, and clean the area of any dried matter until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a tooth grows on the gums, which the elders call «albulus»; one should hold it with tweezers and cut at its root, and let the blood or puss flow; then place powdered vitriol or other binding and dessicating powders over the site; and if that tooth comes back after the incision, and this happens many times, then cut it again and cauterize it: if it does not come back after cauterization, then it will not return. These are the forms of treatment for teeth.
des sordens	of the eyes
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, and there are ugly and rough growths; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, as far as the corruption extends to the gum, and the teeth stink; so one should have the patient hold his head steady with his jaw in your lap, and you should pick at the teeth or growths that are visible, until nothing remains; and thus you should do with the blackness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are all cleaned out; and if it is removed on the first attempt, that is good; if not, then one must repeat the procedure again the next day or the third, until everything is cleaned out; and know that teeth require diverse forms of tools for cleaning, according to what the work demonstrates, so that the pick used to clean between the teeth has different forms from those used to clean the teeth themselves; and these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure a tooth of its pain, you should hurry to pull it out as far as you can, because one must not delay in doing so; for there is no excuse for not pulling it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to draw breath, you must be certain of the tooth that hurts. Many times, the pain deceives the patient and makes them believe it is in the good tooth, and they have the healthy tooth pulled; and yet the pain does not go away through this, as long as the bad tooth remains, for we have already seen this happen to these patients. And when you are certain of the tooth that hurts, you must scrape around the tooth all around to the gum; then open your mouth wide to push back the gums on all sides; then move it with your fingers or with fine tweezers, little by little, until it is well loosened; then grip tightly with the tweezers. And the head of the patient should be held firmly between your knees so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Then pull the tooth straight out without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and rotten, you must fill the holes with cotton, where the rottenness is; and grip it gently with tweezers so that it does not break while being pulled out; and you must work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part of it behind, which often brings greater pain to the patient due to the root remaining. And be aware that you do not do as the ignorant healers do, who sometimes break the tooth while pulling it out because of their haste and force; they do not pay attention to what we have just described, and sometimes bring about a serious illness due to the roots left behind, or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. After the tooth is pulled, wash the socket with wine, or garlic and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of forceps, which are silent in the teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so they do not double when you pull the tooth. And these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made of iron, and they should be toothed to hold the roots.
de la racine des dens	of the root of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains when pulling, you should put wet cotton on the spot for one or two days until the gums are softened. Then use forceps called "algefri", which make the gums look like a sow's mouth; they should be made inside as well as a file, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, you must uncover the skin all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", which is made of ivory, thus its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, whose forms come later:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one should also use this instrument with .ij. tweezers, of which the form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are before in the reason of teeth, and with this instrument that resembles a large pair of tweezers, of which the form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be outside so that it does not break, and know that there are many instruments of teeth; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise subtle master finds his own instrument by himself, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are some diseases in which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if it does not break from the carriage or other bones, or it protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, that I have told you about, and helps with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but he can hold and remove it; and then restore the site with appropriate medicines, and if there is protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then he should treat it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to nature and its shape is ugly, especially in virgins, then you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be filed or polished; then pull it out; and if there is air with the tooth, take this instrument of which here is the form, and it is like a small beak, and let it be of iron sharpened at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And pull it gently day by day because of the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others; and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with a type of file like this:
