et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the lime that needles are made from; and with the lime, lightly prick the tooth little by little, so that it does not move until it chips; then smooth it at the end with a file completely, and if the tooth is too sharp and bites into the tongue, then file down the sharpness so that it neither bites nor corrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, either through concussion or biting down, and the patient cannot press down on what they are eating without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, for silver wires turn green and rust, but gold never moves. The wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth. Then, if you wish to direct the teeth, take the wire and loop it twice between two healthy teeth; then place the ends between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, as far as you can reach without bleeding. Then return to the starting point and gently pull your hand upwards so that nothing moves, and ensure that the wire is pressed against the tooth root so it cannot escape. Then twist the wire ends with pliers, bring them together, and place them between the healthy teeth so they do not bite into the tongue. Leave it tightly in place as long as it will stay, and if it comes undone or the wires break, then restrain it with another wire. It will remain this way all his life, and this is the shape of the teeth and how to adjust the two healthy teeth:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth chips, if it is put back in its place, freshly and as we have said; and only a wise and experienced person should attempt this, and sometimes one makes the shape of a tooth out of cow's bone, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and restrains it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the vein of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	At times this vein, which comes from under the tongue, is natural and present since birth; sometimes it occurs due to a wound. The treatment is as follows: open the mouth of the patient, place their head in your lap, and lift the tongue. Then cover the nervous vein broadly so that the tongue is dislodged from its position. If there is hardening or a lump due to a wound, insert the claw and cover the vein broadly; be careful not to cut too deeply into the artery underneath. Once you are done, apply aqua rosa or aqua frigida, and then place a tent made of linen under the tongue. Apply theriac to the patient every night so that the vein does not heal and become joined again. If there is any bleeding, apply ground vitriol; if the bleeding persists, cauterize it with a lentigo cautery, which is suitable for this purpose. Then treat the wound with other treatments until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it discolored to a dusky or black color, and the patient does not feel any pain, do not touch it because it is a ulcer. If it is declining towards a phlegmon and there is moisture, insert the claw and open it with a spatulum, releasing it from both sides. If bleeding occurs due to your action, apply ground vitriol until it stops; then return to your treatment, continuing until you have removed everything. Afterwards, apply aqua rosa and aqua silice, and treat the wound with other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are sometimes growths in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called tonsils. When you treat them as we have described in the section on tonsillitis, and they do not heal, pay attention: if they are small, hard abscesses with a yellowish color, do not touch them with iron. And if it is red and the root is swollen, do not touch it with iron either, so that blood can flow; but let it be until it heals, then you will split it open, or it will burst on its own. If it is white and the root is thin, prepare an instrument for cauterization, but first check to see if the abscess has cooled down and is calm. Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head should be in your lap, with his mouth open and the servant gripping his hands tightly, and press the tongue down under the entire instrument, which should be made of silver or thin bronze like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	While pressing the tongue with this instrument, you will see the abscess. Take a pair of tweezers and grab it, then pull it up into the tonsil and out from the top as hard as you can; pull some of the threads along with it, then cover the instrument with a cloth, which is part of its shape, so that it looks like a fork. The prongs are curved, one facing one way and the other facing the opposite way, and they are very sharp, made from iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, use a pair of tongs with the same shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it has a sharp edge on one side and a flat edge on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and with water and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water, or with peels of pomegranates that have been cooked, or with bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them then just as the two tonsils are cut.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat; it was specifically one small abscess. Her throat was almost completely closed, so the woman could not breathe through the passageway that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died within a day or two. The abscess had grown so much that it had pushed out two of her tonsils. I quickly inserted an awl into one of the openings of the tonsils, then pulled it towards me, removing a large amount of pus; I then did the same on the other side, opening up her mouth and pressing her tongue. Afterwards, I inserted the awl into the abscess and cut out a portion of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the passageway in her throat was opened, and she began to drink water and wine. I continued to cut into the abscess for a long time, and it would grow again and fill up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large. So, I packed it with medicine and cauterized it inside her throat; in this way, it stopped growing. I left those parts, and she remained under the care of God after me.
de l’uve	from the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye descends to the uvula, and it is swollen and long, it is called 'perpendicular'; and if it is thick and round, it is called an 'eye'. When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the pain of the throat has subsided, and it is thin; and it is round and not long; and it is blood-red, or dark red, or black, then you should make an incision. For there is great danger in this disease. Therefore, when you see it according to the manner I have described, from its whiteness and length, let the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and pull it down, and cauterize it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for the incision of the two almonds. You must not cauterize more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit, because if you cauterize too much, it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said about the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it heals. And if the patient fears the cautery, then you should use a sedative for the cautery without fear. The manner of the cautery is as follows: the patient puts his head down, and then presses his tongue against the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and it is applied with live coals so that it is not too thick or too thin; and with this instrument, which has this shape,
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and has a handle on the top where one puts the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and one places the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and mucous flow from his mouth due to the medicine, so that it does not descend into the throat and cause bleeding; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for the amount of half an hour, until you see it becoming numb and the bites of the medicine calm down; and if you see [this], take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument all the way into the eye with the cotton on top, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after 4 or 5 days. And if you need to repeat the cautery of the medicine, then repeat it, and after the cautery, wash around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and use rosewater, and cure it with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, avens, and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put garlic in it, and let it boil; and the pot should be well-glazed with strong clay, and in the pot there is one instrument with a handle according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it can be of silver or bronze, and the patient's head is pushed into the mouth so that the vapour rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is numbed; then do this often until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, for many things can happen; nor should this be done after the hot abscess has subsided. And if this instrument is not available, take a tube and put an egg yolk inside it, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for the egg yolk does not let the vapour harm the mouth, and this is a good remedy altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, becomes stuck in the throat; therefore you must try to pull it out as far as you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all your strength, so that you can feel the object moving; and if it does not come loose and remains stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit until the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting. Or let the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel-wool, or a lettuce root, or a dry crumb of bread; and tie a string to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it reaches the spot, it will lodge there, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have described, take a leaden instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be bent at one end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the upper part lifted up; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest you harm it, nor push the bone in; and move the patient's head so that he vomits, in order for the object to come out; then let him swallow the instrument again, or pull it out with the instrument, equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	When the blood is treated with medicine, as I have said in the division, by the cure of remedies, and if this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about. And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook, or with fine tweezers suitable for this. And if this doesn't work, take a thin, curved needle, and insert it into the throat of the patient, then heat the needle, and do this frequently. And if the patient is suffering from a cold all day, then take a full glass of cold water, open his mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, moving it around with his hand frequently; and as soon as the blood meets the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not stop as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida using the instrument I described for smoking out the throat; do this many times, for it will work without delay. And the way to smoke it is to put burning charcoal in a pot, and cover the pot with a perforated lid, and insert the tip of the instrument into the hole; then blow your smoke into the pot, and have the patient put the end of the needle in his mouth, close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but goes to the blood; and the blood will stop now, and if it does not, then repeat the smoking many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salty and sour things, and drink no water; and then he will surely urinate.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the throat looks like bent tongs so as to be able to enter the throat; it resembles a bird's beak and has roughness from sandpaper so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; see the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what the following recollections come from here and there in this book; and they differ in penetration and size. And they come in two ways: one is in its appearance itself, and the other is where they are located in the body. For example, an abscess in the head is different from one in the fundament, and an abscess in fleshy tissue is different from one that occurs in joints; each requires a different treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there is an abscess that one must not pierce until the boil is ripe according to its maturity; and there are some that one must pierce when they become crusty without waiting for their maturity, as with abscesses near joints. For when abscesses occur near joints, and you leave them until they are purulent around the joint, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become corrupted due to the pressure, causing contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is near a principal organ, and you delay piercing it until it is mature; it will harm the principal organ. But one must not pierce an abscess with a crust without digestion being complete, except for the one near the fundament, which may become elongated inside and cause a fistula; it will not heal quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of the piercing of the abscess which is dead according to its maturity, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the diminishment of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the piercing in the most dependent place of the abscess, and where it appears soft; and let the piercing be deep in the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and on nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In places that fold, according to the part of the body. And when abscesses are in fleshy places, it is good that you leave the piercing until there is complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce them too early, they will discharge poison throughout the body, and they fill with much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths will harden. And one must treat small abscesses with small holes, and large abscesses with large holes, and many slits according to the appearance of their size; and in some abscesses one must cut out the core, and cover them when they have become as soft as a pad, and are dead, as one does with blisters. And there are some that split into three angles, and some which are covered like the leaf of a bay tree, as with abscesses of the veins; and there are some on which one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those which have no head, like a superficial abscess, you must pierce directly; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at once, but some part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this several times until all the pus comes out. Do this especially when the patient is weak in strength, or a woman carrying a child, or a small child, or an old person. For sometimes the patient will jump with the discharge of pus and die without you realizing it. Therefore be very careful with this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, wash the wound, and if the wound of the abscess is small, then dress it with linen tenting; and if it is a large abscess with many holes, then insert a tent into each one so that they touch each other; and if you have cut into the skin and removed some, then fill it up with old cotton or rag without moisture, and leave it for three days, then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If bleeding occurs due to your work, apply cold water and ease, and moisten a cloth, placing it over the bleeding area many times. If the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and use the powders I have described earlier in this book. If it is winter, and the abscess is very nervous, you should place tents and moistened cloths in warm wine and oil over it; if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, you should place moistened cloths in water and oil, or cool wine and oil, for a third of a day, as we have said. Then open the abscess, wash and care for it, as it should be, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now you should know generally about the treatment of abscesses. I have told you how one must proceed before treating abscesses, and you have the chapter here.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Or, when the head comes from small abscesses, and they are handled like those in woven cloth, as is the jaw of a young girl, and there are many varieties of them. There are some that are fatty and some that are piercing in shape, and there is no doubt if the artery doesn't act contrary. And the treatment for the neck is to examine it with all possible instruments called "endoscopers", from which the form comes afterwards, indicating what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then pierce it from above. And when the moisture has been discharged, then scorch it without leaving any of the skin that contained the moisture, for it will return to being sore if anything is left; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and let it be until the next day; and continue this way for those who are staying overnight. Then on the second and third days, repeat with the cotton as before, as long as you know well that nothing is left overnight; then care for the wound with suitable ointment until it is healed. And if the abscess contains a fatty lump, cut it according to its shape; pierce and scrape all around, and put all your treatment into drawing out the lump where it lies; and if the artery acts contrary, do as I have told you after. And do the same for an abscess that is hard in texture and shape, curing
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision on a stone-like, moist abscess is lighter, because there is little blood in it. And if some of these abscesses are found in the head or where there is no moisture, and there was such an abscess that I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had cut into any of them, they would have made a wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, the opening should be in the most dependent place all day long so that the pus can drain out; and treat them as it should be done.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses come on the neck, and under the armpits, and sometimes in other parts of the body, and they are very common, and are intertwined with each other. And each scrophule is properly within its coat, just as the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrophules. There are some which contain moisture, and some which are malignant and do not respond to treatment. So, when you see one with a good disposition for cutting, and it looks like the color of the body, and it is smooth in each part and is not ulcerated at the nerves of the neck or at the artery or duct, and is not deep; then you should cut it from above, and peel it from every side, and the two lips of the wound should be pinched together, if necessary, as we have said for abscesses of the head; and drain it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut into any nerve or vein, and do not use too much force, so that the hand does not slip, and do not cut too deep.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it will not let you work, then put into the wound powdered vitriol, or some powder that stops bleeding, and bind the wound tightly; and leave it until the abscess is relieved, and the wound softens, and begins to discharge pus. And when the blood is stanched, return to your work, until you finish it; then examine with your finger if there remains any small scrofula, cut it out and cleanse it. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, do not cut out that scrofula at its root, but ligate it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton saturated in Egyptian ointment, and then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out all the scrofula, then it is necessary to bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that no superfluity remains due to the size of the scrofula; then it is necessary to attend to stopping the root of it, drawing it out and sewing as we have said. Those scrofulae that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears dead; and pierce thus as that one before was said, depending on it, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is left of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, cure it with ointment smeared on charcoal, until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of throat surgery, but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with scrofula, the flap of flesh in the throat called the "epiglottis" should be cut away; and this is done to help those with an abscess that is hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.Si li maladie est en la gorge, il covient que tu fendures la gorge et li pormon dou costé, car il ne peut aler si non.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to split the epiglottis, we should split it underneath three or four small splits, across two circles, or according to the size of the split in the hyoid, but not into the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places where it is suitable to cut the epiglottis so that there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long in between.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the teacher is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat to the end, then cut the cartilage as far as it goes to the cartilage; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the hyoid, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the cartilage that it jumps up due to the place which is broken, and due to the defect in the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open to the air.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and sew it up completely without the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient judged dead, and the lack of breath evident.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, grab the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he will breathe through the wound, and thus be saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the maliciousness of the disease has passed, and it is passed in 3 or 4 days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a damsel take a knife and stab herself in the throat, cutting through part of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and I found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that blood had issued from it, and I judged that she had not coughed up any blood or vomited anything other than through her throat, and the blood was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound and healed it until it was cured;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the lady had no worse than a hoarse voice, and she recovered and returned to her senses;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for this reason, I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis one shouldn't have fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess colored yellow, and it often occurs in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and there are two types: natural and accidental; the natural type has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are according to two methods, one of which resembles grease, and the other method resembles an abscess that comes out of our veins;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it has fear, and one should not work with fire except in a small one, and test and search throughout the orifice;
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as soft as grease, and it cannot move at all, so grab it, just as one grabs nuts, and pull it to the top of its neck, if there is nothing there;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search thoroughly, and treat it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of doing this, and I will tell you all about them.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Now I must tell you all the difference between a natural birth and a caesarean section.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that childbirth is a fever and heat that lasts until the delivery is complete and the placenta is expelled; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With no heat or fever or pain, and it contains a pustule, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a boil, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their appearances, either dry or moist, and their colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the pustule, that you examine and inquire into it first with all the instruments called "entromissoires", according to what its form will allow, as described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of the inquiry into pustules on the head is that you press in the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers a little bit by little bit, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the instrument, and take care that nothing jumps out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If pus runs clear, whatever color it has, treat it as I have described for other abscesses:
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the instrument no pus comes out, know that it is fat, so treat it in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side and guard the skin where it lies so that you draw it clean with the needle;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it clean, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if he remains untouched, he will return many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if he stays a little while and the wound does not trouble him, then employ some corrosive powders on the wound, and bind it up, and apply healing remedies to the abscess until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the edges of the wound, and treat it with an ointment that promotes flesh growth.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound is bleeding profusely or otherwise behaving contrary to how it should, then hasten and apply ground vitriol, and leave it for two or three days until the wound scabs over; then return to using what was previously effective.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the probing instruments, and they come in three varieties: large, medium, and small. And there are three types of probe tips: one is called "albaret", and another is called "breb". There are also three sizes of these probes: large, medium, and small, for probing abscesses and fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are similar to the needles used for sewing sorcery dolls, made of brass, iron, or silver. The yellow-colored ones are more effective and are often treated with black pitch to probe the curves of fistulas.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the aperture.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the knives are very varied, as you can see here: large, medium, and small. Some knives have two curves in three ways.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and if they have three curvatures, and are also in three ways; and if they have two curvatures, and only one curvature, and are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of those that have hooks are cutting, and there are some that do not cut except on one side, which scratch the brain, so that they do not cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and with these introducers are the leeches applied in many ways so that the patient does not perceive it when opening abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are in three ways: large, small and medium, as you can see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and don't use it anywhere except in fleshy places, like legs, and arms, and breasts, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling a piece of wood, according to this form, with which blood is stanched;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and sometimes it is placed in the place that heals by opening veins and arteries, and sometimes they are bound according to this large form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they become corrupt, so that they seem like a woman's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must bleed according to this form from b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat away, and fill the wound with medicine made from charcoal, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and let it heal;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags downward and becomes softened due to its size as it does with women, then make two cuts above, along two similar lines;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one line holds the other at its end, and the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from b. to g.:
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, and what is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient will not rest, or due to blood flow, then you must fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it remain until it absorbs the residue and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come under the armpits are types of hard scrofula where there are nodules, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore which contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels which are in the abscess have been emptied, employ the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat it with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of scrofula, they should proceed as we have said in slits for scrofula; and if the wound becomes swollen, they should apply cauterization as we have said previously.Et se li apostemes est desoz le col ou desoz les asseles, si covient que il soit fendu a la radice selonc la ligne m. jusc’a la ligne .g., car en cest lieu il conviens que il soit fenduz selonc la ligne de la nature.
de la routure de l’artere	on the rot of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is rotted and the skin above it is sewn together, this often results in abscesses forming. This also happens when there is swelling of a vein and an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows it thus when it is from the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a constriction. And when it is from the vein, there is a swelling and a appearing of heat.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is madness to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the armpit and in the groin and neck and many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore one should avoid the cautery of iron, and that which is on the head should also be avoided, as well as that which is due to inflammation of the artery, which pierces through the skin of the neck.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then cut into the armpit, and carefully separate the artery from the lymph nodes, so that it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then push a needle under the artery and pierce it all the way to the other side, and compress the artery with a double thread about six inches long, according to what I have instructed you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then point to the spot between the two threads of an introducer so that the pus comes out and the abscess is drained;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the ointment in a circular motion, until the thread moves freely;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply the appropriate ointment, until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to an open wound, you should dye the entire area around the wound with the pus,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then take the needle in the hand you are using to hold it and make the incision there, and thread it with a double length of thread so that you can pull it through from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then ligature the abscess, as I have told you, either with one part of the double thread or with both parts;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you are afraid that the thread will slip out, then tie another needle to the single thread all the way under the abscess at the incision of the first needle and pull the threads tight in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess so that the excess fluid drains out, then cut away the excess fluid from the skin and leave what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer tenting treatments and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the arteries and veins, they come to the nerves when they are wounded, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often at the shoulders and elbows and in all places where there are joints, and it is a kind of abscess, and its colour resembles that of the body, and it has various dispositions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is pulled firmly, the patient feels pain, but it is not located throughout the body, but beneath the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it is mute in all parts, and cannot go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and that which is in the joints must not be covered with iron; there might be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are on the head or forehead, cut the skin at the temple.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, grasp it with tweezers and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, they suspend it from the hook, then scrape it, and the bone and stitch up the wound until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large bumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it occurs in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called 'fungus' because of its resemblance to oats, and it has a fine root and the bumps are large; and there are small ones and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a man who had 2 of these in his belly which looked more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were soft and oozing fluid.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I copied and found in one 18 ounces weight, and in the other 6 ounces, and the operations in the incision are such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with a fine root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the incision is made too wide, and the cautery tools are ready in front of you. For there are often great blood losses when cutting, and if the blood flows out, then hurry with the cauterization;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with the iron, then take a well-made piece of plaster and apply it to the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days;et se li sans ne vient pas adous, si le contremande a son maistre, qu’il ne te vienne a l’incision, por ce que li sans ne vienne adous, tant come li sans soit contremandé.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it and do not stop pressing the plaster on the joint until it is cut through; if the roots are large, they may have fear of cutting it directly through the belly, but you can cut halfway through it,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cover the thalamus which is of a dusky color and poor sense, and milk-like appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer next.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or cut on the syphilis, and is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other routings, or from blood that comes from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is through the rupture of the soft tissue and through the opening of the hernia, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens with multiple openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then it is more varied; and when one presses it with their hands, it retreats, and then comes back out, and sometimes it is blocked, and increases significantly at the entrance of the bath and with intense effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a minor issue, and opens easily when you press it with your hand, and does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, then it opens through these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to ventosities, then there is swelling on the touch, and the actions are such that you should observe whether the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or ventosities.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	If you should let it heal. For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the swelling is in the intestines or the belly, then you should instruct the patient to tighten his belt and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the abdomen;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to sit up quickly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the area that you have signed all around the spasm,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	and the half of the abscess above the great toe;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tightly bind it with a strong thread or a strong silk cord, and the patient must abstain from sexual intercourse;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open the half of the abscess that extends above the ligature, and push in your finger, and probe the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught by the ligature, then loosen it and push the intestine back into the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the boil, they take it at the root and cut off the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery causes contrary results, or the vein, go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, thread them with two strong threads, and insert the two needles into what you have pierced in a cross pattern;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then press the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you see that it is coming out, remove the needles, and leave the wound to drain until it can heal;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you can cut it when it is thin and draining, then clean the wound as needed, and treat the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture which you find, then treat the area as appropriate, and close up the wound.
dou chancre	from sores
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the likenesses of sores, and how one should work with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure by iron; and we speak of sores which are found in the genitals, and great caution is needed in their treatment. The ancient ones say that when sores are in a place where they can be scratched, like sores found on breasts, or thighs, or similar places, then one should completely remove them when they are in their beginning stage. But when they are large and old, one should not touch them, for I have never been able to heal any such sores, nor has anyone healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
