Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come by birth, or by wound, or by burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	Then you must treat this wound so that the bones heal according to their natural shape.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tent or damp cloth soaked in rose oil, so that it does not clot;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you can place between two thin pieces of wood, until the wound is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a person with a sore palm comes to you, then treat that wound as it should be treated.
Des vils	Of the poor
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Fists are large, wrapped vesicles full of melancholy humors that come from various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in other people.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him an emetic, and then the basil drink.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	There are two methods of treatment with fire. One is to cut and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The other method is to open a vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision is performed in the following manner: first, heat the leg with very hot water until the large veins are made smaller.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then, press the leg of the patient from above the thigh to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then open the vein in one place, or two or three places, with a wide cut,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then squeeze and draw out the black blood into your hand from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to drink possets of black wine;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the bleeding and purging when the veins are full, and ease the patient's pain.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatments for dislocation are as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then place it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it by fire, and then apply the hot compress directly to the vein from the top of the ankle down to the knee, or in the area below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the joint, and scorch the vein on each side, until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it appears as a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then it goes under the skin until it is elevated, and then it can be easily removed with tweezers,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut into another area above the vein in three places; then scorch the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up with tweezers, as you have done before, and remove it with another pair of tweezers, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another strip, or several if you need them, then lift it, and place it on the bottom of the foot
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull and lift it up to the second strip; then pull it out from strip to strip, until it comes all the way out, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot pull and lift it, then thread a strong doubled thread through it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	Tie it and pull it, and insert a needle under it, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and make sure it doesn't pop out, for if it pops out, one cannot milk or lift it, and harm comes to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished milking, place on the site of the wound a damp cloth soaked in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the shoulder is contracted, crooked and wrapped together, not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	you should split it crookedly but not pop it; and milk it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife with which one cuts the vein is curved, and it does not cut unless it touches the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it has a large curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein; but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is angular in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and occasionally they grow elsewhere than on the legs; and this happens due to a pustule that forms under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as snakes and worms enter the body between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a great inflammation in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the color changes, and the vein begins to emerge, just as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is exposed, you must wrap it around with a piece of linen one and a half yards long, and tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the linen hanging down to the leg, and every time he feels a discharge, wrap it around again with the linen, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining part around, and do not cover the root at all until it is completely discharged.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cover it, it will enter the body and cause abscesses and pustules in that place, and a serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	it must be treated little by little until it reaches the head, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein is treated from five to ten inches long, or more,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once a man came to me whose vein was as long as ten inches, and when you cut it, it gushed out like a spring, and penetrated all the way to the bone,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all the matter inside is drained out, and then apply healing medicines for several days, just as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein bleeds profusely, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot, or in the foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and from which it shoots out blood; treat it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that grow between skin and flesh:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land, because it often happens to oxen:
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and there is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and travels through the body going up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and can be felt moving from one part of the body to another until it breaks through the skin where it is going, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by certain humors, like worms and serpents and roundworms and tapeworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one suspects its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled, one cannot hold back tears when he sees it:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so you must tie the area above and below with a strong string, tied tightly,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut it on top and pull it out hard, and if the pus is deep in the flesh and you do not release it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize with fire above it, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then press firmly under the eyebrow, then pull upwards and out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	It is necessary to use a cleansing agent for the body with medicinal solutions to draw out the bad humours,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and from foods that cause constipation.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from wind.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in some parts of the body,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and can move from one part of the body to another; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she exposed her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise up like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything else, as bright and lively as silver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that spot and moved to the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she started to turn around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved from limb to limb like that, because I had never seen this illness behave in that way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I have not seen it in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought it was because women had dry skin and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason the wind is forced out.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and have moist skin and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	examine it thoroughly above and below, then press on until that windiness is forced out of its place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the remedy for those windinesses, like foul-smelling pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and the place in the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their heads is such that there are those with large points, small ones, smooth ones, and serrated ones.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those who have .ij. angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which falls in any member falls according to .ij. ways: or in the principal member falls,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as brain, heart, liver, lung, intestines, bladder and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore falls in any of these members, and the sign of death which I will tell you about later becomes apparent to you:The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must be wary of extracting this arrow, for death comes afterward in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign is not apparent and the arrow is not deeply lodged, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the spinal fluid leaks out from above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is vomiting and vomiting of blood, and blackness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness in the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps this happens without blood coming from the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is moisture coming out of the wound like pus, and also like blood;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear, then cease the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not stuck.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of a wound when it falls on the heart are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as though it were pierced into something hard, and not hollow;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and occasionally the patient becomes mute like the poultry, and turns pale with black blood, and experiences chilliness and cold sweat, and faints:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without a doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that never leaves the body is foam without pain, emerging from the wound, and a swollen throat, and the patient's colour changing, and gasping for breath and seeking the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits in the groin area, between the ribs; and it causes great pain and suffering, and gasping; and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces the heart or stomach, by chance something indigestible may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the belly and nothing comes out through the intestines but feces, there is no hope for a cure nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and urine comes out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that this wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, buttock, thigh, and leg, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and is not poisonous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man that an arrow struck him in the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it and drew it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I extracted an arrow that had struck him in the fatty tissue under the eyeball, below the eyelid:
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow had been removed, but only the tip was protruding from the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large, shot from a Turkish bow, and had a broad head without ears; the player was unharmed, and no ill fate befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	He then shot an arrow at a Christian's throat, and the arrow had Arabic writing on it with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut off their beards and throttled them until I killed them, and the Christians were unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew an arrow from a man who had it in his head or belly, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and removed it, and he had no bad reaction.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man who has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound is sewn up over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and left the arrow inside him, and did not change his natural dispositions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man who had an arrow shot into his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And drew an arrow from the king's head, where it was lodged in the brain,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was somewhat inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely drawn out
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to attend after she had been healed for three days. I found the wound much improved.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined her thoroughly and found no trace of it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed a cooling and digestive plaster on the spot, because the ears were swollen;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the tip of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the ointment repeatedly, re-opened the wound directly, and kept the patient's condition for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied medicine with a corrosive agent to the wound repeatedly, as long as it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow which protruded from the wound;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjusted in the opening of the wound by that medicine water, so that the head of the arrow appeared to me visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and surpassed the boundaries within four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I opened the wound with tweezers, and squeezed it from both sides, but it would not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	so I continued to subtlely and skillfully use tools in various ways, until one day I took well-made tweezers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what his condition will be at the end of this chapter, as I have described it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was sewed up and the patient completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you about the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your treatment on that which I do not say, for books cannot understand everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters understand little about very few things, and what they do know is only what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	they discover new works, and nine instruments, and the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the members where they are lodged in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place they enter, or elsewhere;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and those that come out through the place they entered, are arrows entering the flesh, and sometimes they come out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, let it be left until the flesh around it is rotted away, and the passageway is cleared;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is lodged in the bone and cannot exit, let it be left for several days, moving it a little each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, then pierce around with a very thin stick until the area around it is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow has pierced into the bone of the head and goes towards one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned are apparent in the patient: then do not pull it out at all, but leave it until it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes to the sinew, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not stuck just in the bone, but goes no further than the sinew,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without ill effect, then use the technique of extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot be removed, then administer cauterization around the wound, as I have told you; then clean the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deep within the body so that it cannot be seen, then look for it throughout the body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then treat it with an appropriate instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then cut it so that the wound is large enough;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears in the arrowhead to which it is attached,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you pull the hair that is stuck in the wound with tweezers as much as you can
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then bend or twist the head of the arrow, so that you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot extract it in one go, then leave it until the surrounding area becomes swollen; then pull it out, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes it contrary, then apply what we have said about treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against cutting the nerve and opening a vein, and use any means you can to draw out the arrow without danger,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and adjust the patient according to the position he was in when the arrow struck him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the greatest aid you can provide; and if you cannot, then adjust him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows which come from another direction, where something sticks out of them, or the skin is swollen in the affected area, either seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut above it, as far as the forceps can reach, and then extract it; if it does not come out immediately, cut again.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand rapidly, so that it goes into the bone and widens the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then try to extract it again until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrow in it, then plug up the entire shaft.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft is broken, and you see a need to administer relief, then administer .i. instrument chewed,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the gum of the instrument; and then plug it out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is chewed, then plug in .i. instrument with a point entering in, to alleviate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow has touched the skin, then you must cup around the entire area where the venom is, as much as you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits the foot, or stomach, or belly, or bladder, or side, and it is superficial, and you can cup over it, then cup over it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cup the vein and nerve, and then pull out the arrow, and then cut the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat until healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the head should be like a bird's feather,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the point of the arrow, as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and probing if it's there:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the common body:
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Veins from which one is healed are .xxx, from which it has in the head xvi.,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Here is the translation:
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries in the two temples, which are visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is in the head of the penis;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips on the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augerich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and 2 veins that are under the tongue
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the one is cephalic, and is on the left side, and people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle vein is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and people call it  "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and people call it  "vein of the belly", and it is above the bladder,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and is that which heals, which is clearly visible above the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvatrix is the vein between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	In the leg there are three veins: one is under the fold of the scrotum on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second superficial vein which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called 'nesse', which is at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and three veins beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding from the veins that are behind the ears helps with old cataracts and with emigration [of the eye].
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the bleeder, as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then strangle the patient's neck with a rope,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	that the .ii. veins appear behind the ears, descending from the head in two places:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	so you will feel the pulse underneath your toe, and if it hurts when you press on it;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and pierce under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand up along the vein;
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through the skin and vein well .ii. times through, and let the blood out until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then I stretch and tie it, until it is healed
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incisions and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding from the two arteries in the temples, which is good for old migraines,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and for sore eyes and accustomed tears in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the surgeon are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels pain under your jaw, and then sign here;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then gently press the vein above your index finger, and insert the lance below,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and open the vein at the top, and the scrotum, as you have done in the two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then ligate it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and extraction in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the frontal vein is as good as the bleeding from the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and when the quality is such that the patient turns his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "forceps", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, and let the blood flow according to the amount you want.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is healthy and sometimes use a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too sharp, and the wound should not be too deep, for the bone is near, and by chance the flames might break when they are thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The wounds of the two veins that are in the two arms help themselves, and also the tinea, and the redness, and the orifice in the eye, and the diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And their quality is that the patient turns his neck to the side by twisting some ligament, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then he cuts it, and it should be cut across, with the flame a little long and wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance it will break; then make the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind it with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding from the vein in the nose is good for nosebleeds, and sudden fainting, and diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient tilts his neck, then he pulls his nose to the left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the thin flame, long and narrow, and insert it between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open easily, and the blood will begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go in too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for a night, for it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is how you make the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The healing of the two testicles helps with the contraction of the anus, and with the beginning of menstruation, and with many illnesses, and with impetigo, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and with ulcers.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the healing is such that the patient stretches his neck back and forth, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the doctor stand above the patient's head, and the patient lie on his back.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the vein a little widely, then draw the blood in a tempered way, or as much as is needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do another turn on the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and gently constrict both veins.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	let the patient not be strangled by it; and leave it until morning when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins of the lips above helps with cold in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and toothache and pain in the jaw.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is to have the patient sit before you, and tighten his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and know them by their being black, and by there being around them fine black veins;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then cut both of them, and if you do not know which to cut and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	take the thickest of each part, and do likewise with the .ii. veins above and below, for it is one and the same procedure.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	On bleeding under the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Bleeding the veins under the tongue helps after bleeding the cephalic vein, and it is useful for tightening the throat, and for diseases of the gullet and mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the bleeding are such that the patient should hold his hands in front of the sun, and stick out his tongue, and look underneath each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then cleanse both of them and do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	Veins of the neck from which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either with a single large silver needle or a thin olive-shaped one with a pointed tip, and it is called «anesil»;
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and slender according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame martin is very renowned, and it is broad as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth and filled with thick blood, and which contain thick and troubled blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed and is for bleeding subtle veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed the basilic vein, and be wary of the artery underneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he pierces the artery, and blood flows out, then he should stanch it as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not pierce the vein, but cut it like an onion.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil doesn't open clearly, then you must extract it and replace it with another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you can tie some of it off, or you can heal the vein in its place in the arm: it will open clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the cautery to the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the location of the bleeding, then you must also stretch out the arm and touch the area until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the place with a cut, then tie the arm, and press the vein with the flame of the cautery;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware of cutting into the artery when you see it swelling, for that is an artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rising upwards as urine does in a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	then hurry and place your finger over it firmly, then remove your finger if the blood stops, for this often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is tied to the arm, and left thus, and the patient should not move it, nor move when it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched and he bleeds and there is no medicine present, then compress the artery where it is cut off, and stop the flow of blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fir, and split it, and take one half and bind it on well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then stop it with a cauterisation, as we have said before, using powders which stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the bandages are not wrapped in various positions because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bleeding from a vein in the middle if it draws blood from the head above and the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the bleeder must be careful not to pierce too deeply and to find the nerve that is underneath,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the saint is distressed, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then you should heal it with the instrument gently; and avoid the nerve as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they cut it from the long one.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sainie of the Cephalic helps, that it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and one must open it with a cautery to the olive flame or the myrrh flame, for it is the safest of all veins, for it has no nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one must seek out the lightest vein, and if one misses it the first time, one should try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes veins will swell for some men, when one misses the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it is not used only to restore health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins: these are the cephalic, the fast, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating when the signs of digestion are apparent;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must bleed the patient the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding administered to the sick has no set time, but when there is need by day or by night, at all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a fetus until the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old be bled who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wishes to cleanse themselves, in whatever way, they must empty the intestines with a gentle enema,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there is fecal matter retained, so that the veins do not draw harmful excess fluids from the intestines to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Neither should one cleanse themselves who is too full of food, nor who is drunk, until they have digested their food and are no longer intoxicated.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one wishes to cleanse after a colic attack, vomiting, and diarrhea, and excessive sexual activity, or from exertion, staying up all night, fasting, or any other activity that weakens the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly draw out the humours, if the illness is severe, through meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter a bath, if nothing else works, to subtly draw out the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and cure the vein of the foot, around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and beware on that day of hard work, and piercing, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be tied and bound, and let the bandage be higher than that of the person being treated, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then loosen the ligature above the wound, for if it is too loose or too tight, it cannot heal.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	Then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then dampen the bandage with a little old oil, then put his index finger of his left hand on the wound under the area he wants to treat,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	that the vein does not burst upon being cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like cords to the heart, and others filled with wind.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	So, if one places it over the flame, it draws in the flame and cannot open the vein, and so it is with some of them.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if the vein opens, the wound is too tight, so one must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, then try again a little lower at the site of the vein or above it, unless the area is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient feels hopeless, then leave it for a day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance, there will be hot abscesses; do not enter into a bath, then start bleeding again if she wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small, cut into it with a sharp knife and you doubt that it won't bleed as much as you want, then pierce that same opening directly with a hot iron.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work on it a little gently, so that the wound is not inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area inflamed, do not re-open the wound, and put on a little linseed oil, because it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the oil that the linseed is made from is useful.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and so use linseed oil in any wound you treat veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this also makes a триачле and bowels of eus, when it is put on the area; so subtlety the blood and splits when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, especially when the wound is not healed but rather small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you have a rush, and put on the spot a sponge wet in water and salt slightly warm, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you should do this after the release of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place for several days with some blackness or greenish color, it will not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on something made of aloe or myrrh dissolved in wine, medicine, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance at the exit of the basilic vein: so put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be careful not to put anything on it from what we have said, because sometimes it cuts through an artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the area, then treat the wound with other treatments until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thinned out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for those who are full and swollen, and need bloodletting, that one makes them a larger wound, and the flames should be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled a little and often, and one must bleed them by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from the long or the wide vein.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for those whose body needs bleeding, one should give them wet bread in pomegranate juice; if they are feverish, they should be bled three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, he should eat before bleeding soft bread dipped in mucilaginous syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and aniseed, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints after the flow of much blood, then he should inhale the steam of warm broth and subtle, scented syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other remedies we have described in the chapter on syncope, for opening a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and bleed again, then when he is weakened by a large bleeding, he should bleed a little at a time according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to open their arm after the first bleeding, and they have strong pulses, then heal for .vii. hours after the first bleeding, or after the new hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another part, then they should bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is a great deal of blood within the body which has become heated, and it brings on fever; therefore one must draw out a large quantity, and widen the orifice so that it drips onto a sponge;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you must observe all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on their pulse when they are bleeding so that death does not come in the place of a sponge,
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and you must not, when you see the arm coming loose and blood coming out a second time, and the wound is closed, press directly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor, if it is crooked, should he stretch out his arm forcefully, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him leave it until it heals the second time; or you put it to the point of the flame, as long as the blood that is congealed at the wound's opening flows out,
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on .I. poultice of celandine, and press it gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and don't constrict it until the abscess is drained.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it's necessary to let blood a second time, then bleed in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	Veins in the arm are bled in the area of the vein near the shoulder because it is closer to the heart.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is for the patient to place his hand in hot water until the fingernails turn red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then he should be left briefly, so that the vein appears well, then he is healed now through the middle, not from the broad or long side;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the incision should be made wide, and he is healed close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, then put the hand in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, because there is more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding from this vein is safer than any other vein, because there are no arteries or nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding to save the right hand is useful for all diseases of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand tightly, and pour in warm water until the vein is swollen, as one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it bleeds sideways, and you bandage it from all sides, it will not hurt at all;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are all stripped of flesh beneath,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	then put the hand in warm water if the blood has congealed in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as necessary, put oil and silk on the vein to heal quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is good for the disease of the mumps, and do everything just as I have told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The treatment for the sore throat is good for all illnesses below the neck.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the kidneys, and of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the nature of its treatment is that the patient puts their foot in warm water, and rubs the sore until it bursts.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the sore is at the ankle, and the swelling goes up above the foot, there are many diseases of the kidneys;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	let them walk in the sun or in the open air, or go barefooted, as they please.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves underneath, and heal it by crossing also as in cupping; and let the flames be mild.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot into water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healing does not work the first time, then try again a second time on top of it, for the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	doubt not to use a nerve, as we have said, and likewise do with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its remedy is for pain in the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And its qualities are such that the patient should enter the bath and twist above the ankle four times in alternation,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it will not open; and if it opens, then remedy it in every way you can, by crossing over and
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better to cut it off, for the head is safe, and she is very relaxed in many men's hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not believe it, then cut a vein on the inside of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and let the blood flow as you wish, then untie the ligature and place cotton on it and tighten it; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of bleeding with leeches:The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suctions cups are made of horn, or brass, or glass; and suction is performed in two ways: by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction without striking is in two ways: either it is with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the suction that is done by striking and drawing blood is made in 14 places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is all in the head; and the other is in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on either side of the neck; and a cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and cupping glasses on the shoulders; and cupping glasses over the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and cupping glasses between the two arms; and cupping glasses between the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and cupping glasses on the ankles; and if no blood is drawn except from small veins that are scattered throughout the body,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore one weakens it not at all, as is done with bleeding of a vein;
