et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and one must not administer it, neither with any fire nor with burning, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if because of necessity of diseases one must blister, or because of habits, then we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between each season.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they have need to blister, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if they experience bloating and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who spit up blood, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed profusely;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who faint, and see blackness, and become weak and die, and experience similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is during the month, we command them to fast after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding of the nose helps the headache that comes from the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this farting is in place of the bleeding of the head,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it should not be used by those of a cold complexion or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason the elderly should not use it, nor those with cool-headed diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal often become blind, and because of this, one must place the cupping glass a little lower down due to the fear of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The location for cupping on the neck is at the junction of the skull and the basilic vein, and because of this, it is useful for constriction of the feet.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for fissures in the gullet, and for toothache, and for bloating;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and one must press it only lightly, because if it holds too tightly, it causes blindness or stomach ache and heart pain.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The wind's ventilation through the .ij. ribs of the neck is good for the pains in the head, and ophthalmia and eye-waterings, and for strangulation, and for toothache at the roots.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of bleeding from the basilic vein; and you must instruct the bleeder to express his hand while placing it, so that he does not grasp the artery and cause a gushing of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation under the chin is good for diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and it is in the place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation of the armpits is good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the armpits is as good as three veins in the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon not to pierce too deeply, because underneath there are nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is placed on the hip is as good for hemorrhoids and diseases underneath, and it should be large, made of copper, and have a strong suction; and perhaps if it were thin, it would break, causing large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg cupping-glasses heal very apparently, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the legs, and in the hips, and in the bladder; and bring back the period, and are placed on the two sciatic nerves and the two ankles, yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping-glass is to place it first empty, and suck gently, and apply it firmly, and move equally, and not cease doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then stop, and remove the cupping-glasses, and take heed in the disposition of the body, for there are some who have such thin skin and wide pores: therefore only strike once, and make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to open the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw blood a little at a time, we only need to strike once.Et se li sans est clers et espés, si convient ferir  .iiij. fois soulement.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, then we open the vein frequently; and if the blood is thick, then heat it until it flows, and the terminations are such that the heart is pierced suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is fitting for those with thick and tough skin, and those with tight pores, that you grease the places where the cupping glasses will be placed with a warming and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is on the neck, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is on the liver, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of amaranth, or of balsamite, or aniseed oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one is healing tender flesh with large pores, then no oil should be applied,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but after venting, they should wash with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if they rise from garlic, or myrrh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large swellings rise from old wine, or from water of soap, or from a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and should not be bled with a cupping-glass before the bath or emetic, but after; and should not sleep after cupping,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is good that he should fast when he is to be bled, and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the patient is choleric and the blood is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if he should press cold things, like pomegranates and endive and lettuce with garlic, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little, and meat broth, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those of a cold complexion should drink honey syrup, and moderate old and new wine, and meat broth, and little birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he is bleeding, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people musk or civet before or after wind-letting, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and dilute the wine, but those who are hot tempered should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are used without bleeding are those that are used on the liver, and on the mumps, and on the scrofula, and on the belly and the armpit, and the rain, and the hip, because these members do not tolerate being bled on the eyes,
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we place cups on the breasts when they are swollen to reduce the swelling in the member, so we place cups on the belly and armpit to make the member smaller.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it relieves the pain when there is gangrene or a stone, and by its attractive power, the gangrene is removed, or the stone leaves its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus it acts when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cups are administered empty to suck only slightly; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as with diseases of the lungs, and in such a way one fills the cupping glass with hot water, or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup to be administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has 2 fingers in width and a half palm in depth, and it has on each side around the middle a small hole, just big enough to push through an awl,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be made of bronze, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a twisted rod of iron or steel to hold a candle
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and both large and small according to the illnesses and ages of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because children's leeches are different from adults', and lean people's different from fat people's.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And it should thus be placed on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle of wax or .i. lining, and put it inside the suction cup through the tube which is inside the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the flame is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be on the hole that we have described, so that when one wishes, the vapors will go in and the suction cup can be removed;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and they take the lining as before, and do it repeatedly if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	Therefore the cupping glass which is applied in case of dropsy, with any acute disease, has no tube or opening, and is not removed until it is full of water, and is placed on the limb alone;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are not removed until in members where one cannot place cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on naked flesh, such as testicles or nipples, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and its use is such that when you find leeches in clean, fresh water without mud, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	place them in clean, fresh water until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then cleanse the wound with a vein-opening poultice and a cupping glass, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the leeches on top;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are swollen and biting, if there is a vein nearby where a cupping glass can be placed, then do so, for it is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the place with ash, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it out.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the bite is too low on the body of the snake, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it there until the fang is extracted;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the fangs are multiple, then apply ground vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until they are extracted;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you can place half a pod of split peas on the site and leave them until they dry out, which will stop the bleeding now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the spot with fresh blood, or stick a needle into it until the leech attaches.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them on the wound, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see them excrete, sprinkle some powdered aloes and salt, or ash on the wound, and they will stop bleeding soon after.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish multitude are ignorant of this chapter, and have never read any ancient books or letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, knowledge is strange in our land, for I found no good ones.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it except through the knowledge gained from ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have attained to a knowledge of them, and by experience, and by the habits of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have summarised it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in the two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue to this book that the subjects of the discussion and the chapters in which the sage places his understanding, and dwells upon the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, or dislocation, or twisting, or a broken bone occurs in anyone, you should hasten to treat the patient from both sides, if nothing else holds them back, such as weakness of body, or youth, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is very hot or too cold; and eat cool foods, that is, cold joints of meat, and venison and kid, and drink no wine, nor eat any fatty meats, nor fill yourself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have a doubt about a hot abscess, or the spread of matter in the limb; then return the patient to their first treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one must feed the patient foods that promote swelling and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testes, pigs' feet, pig's belly, offal, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with more swelling the break will be closed more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and the feeble cannot heal well or join together according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But have no worry, reset it on the broken bone, specifically the large tendons which stretch and join the limb together, as much as it was before; and do not cut off any part of his work, and for this reason he needs to eat lots of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures come in many forms and manners.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg; and I will tell you in this chapter about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture which goes to the bone, and another in puncturing, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break all over a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its own method, and its own proper instrument for healing, according to what memory comes in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that the break of the bone is due to the twisting of the limb, and it is apparent by discolouration, and sounds when pressed by the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or sound upon pressure, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can have tortuosity, or split, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it by hand, but apply the medicines that follow, and then hold it firmly but gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and where the two parts are separated, they must now be put back together evenly, just as in an abscess;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscesses are hot, let it rest for a day or two, until the abscesses are soothed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then you make it even with the muscle that you can easily and gently, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of that in which there are pieces; then you hold it, as appropriate next.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, it is stretched from two parts, whether it is the hand or foot, or to your hand if it is a small member, or with two strings, or with one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you bring them back together by any means you can, and be careful that your action does not cause the patient injury or pain;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you can feel it with your hand if it doesn't seem right; then dress it nicely, and don't pull or press too hard as those do who bring about hot abscesses and contractions in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is healed, then caution the patient well that he doesn't move it, nor while awake or sleeping, turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and be sure to guard against any pain in the limb.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when there is no pain, it is not yet healed, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure it is put back correctly so that no crookedness comes to it when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You should know that broken members are diverse in smallness and size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	Because there are small members, such as fingers and toes and similar: you should wrap these with soft, fine linen.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg: these should be wrapped with a broad and firm bandage, because broad bandages embrace the entire limb and constrict it evenly all around, so that there is no swelling.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wind around it lightweight bandages, 3 or 4 turns depending on the limb, and tighten the hand a little on all the bandage, then go above the fracture and loosen it less than the fracture, so that the fracture is moved away a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage little by little as you press on most of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wind it directly over the broken area.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the area under the fracture and constrict it slightly, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said above in the first bandage.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	put between the lines of flax or cloth until it is all even, then tie it all tightly with a bandage, and then put your stars well made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something to soothe the abscess that is warm and reduces the swelling, and leave it like that for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then put your stars under the bandage, and they should be of a medium size made of linen, or wooden sticks like those used for making clothes smooth, or palm leaves, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but the star that is put on the dislocation should be a bit bigger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as it needs to be for the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it tightly against the bones just as you did at first, then tie a thread around it in the same way as before on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is, the better; and the thread should not be too thin or too thick, but of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the thread is thick, as I have seen foolish people make their laces with twisted cords, and this is a great error, for the lace will not be even if it is too thin, and there should be no more than a finger's width between each bone.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is weak after the stretching in their healthy arms, then place beneath them a pad of linen or other soft cloth so that they do not hurt themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment for it later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that one should not dislocate all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it should not be dislocated until after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the heat of the abscess;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and here is the way of the ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations and twists: you take the flour that is held on the walls of the mill, and cook it with plenty of egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way of restoring fractures in various positions, especially in women and young children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and twist: take 3 parts of barley and ladani and enule and assafetida and gum arabic and mastic, each 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, each 5 parts; alechil 7 parts; and grind them into powder, and mix with plenty of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is useful for twists: take mastic and balm of gilead, each 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, each 8 parts; acacia 6 parts; armenic bole 10 parts, and grind well, and cook with water or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way of plaster for joints and for bones out of their sockets, and to soothe the resulting pain, and shrink the swelling: take fresh lard, and cook it in garlic and oil, and apply it to the affected area. These plasters do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of ointment that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earthworm leaves, and crush them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of ointment for the restoration of broken bones and to reduce swelling of an abscess: take marsh-mallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour, one part each; crush and cook with wine. If the member is inflamed, cook with moist coriander water or water and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of ointment that is stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member: take marsh-mallow roots, and flax seed, borage, melilot, and comfrey, and violet flowers and chamomile, one part each; crush and cook with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, depending on the heat of the member and its comfort.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocras writes in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to restore it other than a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says one should put on the broken member, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that helps with injury and pain: take mugwort and human hair shaved off, or bird feathers, and honey, and mix them together, and make a plaster from it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little after, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, loosen it again in a few days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes in the area, or itching, or discomfort, or swelling, act quickly and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take light cloth, and sponge of sea moistened, and dip it in water, and apply it to the area until the itching stops and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then place a dry cloth over it, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it with a cloth until you are sure the abscess is hot.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and alleviate its pain, then restart the gentle binding, and use a little ointment, but do not bind it as tightly as before; and be subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, and you need ointment and binding, then restart it in the same way as before.Et se li maux sont jai osté dou tout, et li membra sont jai sane, si ne fitz mie ren de la lieure ne de l’emplaustre; mes s’il est encores dolor, et enfleure, et roujor, si fitz ren come tu a fait avant.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if there is nothing of what we have said coming to the member, then do not remove it until after 3, 4, or 5 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, depending on how the fracture is healing and approaching the bone underneath.Et si li maux ne vient encores, et le membre est encores infirme, si fitz ren come tu as fait premierement, et tant que le membre est jai enflé et roux, et dolor;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then restrain him more than before, and increase his food, as I have said before. And if you see the place drier than it should be, know that no healing can come from it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then give him a hot water enema, each time you loosen him, and do this every other day, and ease the pressure a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	through this work, the healing comes to the limb, and quickly heals what the foolish do, who restore the limb crookedly: it is evil, and such work is cowardly, and I see nothing in it but laziness and doing it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with diverse appearances, and their causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, breaking the collarbone all the way to the shoulder blade underneath, as with an axe or staff; this type of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without breaking it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; the wound from these two types of fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a deep impact, or a split or blow from a stone, or falling on stone, or other similar occurrences.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a penetrating fracture which approaches the membrane that is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if it has a wound that is lodged in the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called a "capillary" fracture;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by stone, or by falling, or by a similar object, and it drives the bone fragment inward, and the site of the injury is hairy like the hair on a potter's wheel when they work on the pots; then it enters the bone below.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have moist bones in their heads, like children's skulls;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens with all these types of fractures that small pieces are dislodged as they are, and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the distraction upon them and the examination at night, and by the foul smell that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs it, the black crack appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, take care of the accidents of illness, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of consciousness, and extension, and palpitations, and fever, and eyes popping out and turning red, and others similar in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a miraculous event, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is in winter, then you should remove the foreskin before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, then you should hurry to remove the foreskin before the seventh day so that the tissue underneath the foreskin does not decay and cause the problems we have described.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break in the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the damaged part: and it is necessary that you grip the head of the wounded person, and expose above the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more gently than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if blood flows when uncovering the bone, or a wound is caused, aid it with what is appropriate, and you must fill the area with moistened strips of cloth in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the abscess is soothed and you are sure there is no more blood flow; then begin to remove around the bone, and this can be done in two ways of working: one way is that you cut with a close-fitting bandage in front, and this is the shape
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put on another bandage larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various bandages, some narrow and some wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron; and work gently so that you do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, you should pierce around it, so that you administer cauteries with needles, not so deep that they penetrate through the bone of the skull, and it should have a rim or ring above the point, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each comes in its place into the thickness of the bone, so that you have needles for all the holes; and this is the shape of the three types of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one needle on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then remove the needle somewhere else a little later, and do this all around; then cut into the space between the holes with knives, as thinly and lightly as you can, as we have said, until you draw out the bone in your hand or with some of the instruments that you have, like tweezers or pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and drawn out the bone, it is necessary that you cut away the membrane that is left on the bone with some instrument like an incisive knife, but it should be more thin and flexible than the other knives.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there is anything left of the small bones or any chips, remove them lightly with one of these instruments; then heal the wound with poultices and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen speaks of, which is safer; he praises it highly, and his words are:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture is open and moving; then, when you have uncovered that part, place underneath it the head of this lens-shaped instrument, which has a curved shape.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Do not cut in from the side, but make an incision in the middle of the bone, so that the cutting edge is facing the bone. Then strike it gently with a small mallet, so that you nudge the bone all around gently, and be careful of the membrane underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is loose from the bone, then nudge the bone gently, for there is no pain or fear in nudging the bone.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not go all the way through to the membrane, and the bone is only cut slightly on top, with small pieces, then you should re-examine that roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp rasp, of which you must have several quantities, to use in each place the most suitable one according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	First use the coarse rasps, then the finer ones, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other subtle hairline fractures and breaks, you should treat them according to their nature; and this is not a matter that can be fully explained to one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sinus is exposed, you should cover it with a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it over the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another piece of linen, doubled over twice or thrice, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first piece of linen; and do this as gently as you can so that you don't aggravate the ulcer, then apply another bandage on top, and don't tighten it more than is necessary to hold the dressing in place.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it like this for one or two days, until the abscess is soothed, then remove it and apply medicine made from lilies, wheat flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these ingredients and apply it to the wound, and then administer other medicines without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and take care that the wound is clean and that you don't leave any ointment or pus on it, because when pus collects under the skin's surface, it hardens and causes great harm to the patient; for when one applies something biting to an ulcer, it causes hardening on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if discoloration does not come from the medicine that has been applied, because it has such a virtue, then you should take some honey and mix in three parts rose oil, and stick to a bandage, and place it on the ulcer;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it in ways that are appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken, one by itself, because they are two bones; and below is cartilage, which does not break but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should place your index finger or thumb over the nose, and put the break inside your finger according to its natural shape, and hold it there with pressure until the nose returns to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and make sure the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the elbow and the bone cannot be put in place, then you should place it evenly at the top of a fairly thick rod.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, do the same, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses have healed, then attach to the top of the elbow a tent made of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one from each side, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the bones.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some say that one must soak the bandages in butter, and change them every day. I do not think this is good, but they should be soaked while preparing egg white and flour; then leave the bandage until the bone is set and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts in goose feathers instead of bandages, and on top a silk cloth; and the patient holds it in place, and breathes among them; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if there are abscesses on the nose while you are doing this, put cerotic ointment or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a pouch of diaquilone.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if no pus comes out, then put a plaster on it, made from flour of linseed, and powdered incense, cooked in egg white, then put over it light wicks, and do not bind it too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments for this purpose, then clean the wound, and heal it with healing substances, warm, as in plasters and ointments appropriate to this purpose;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then heal it with tents, and put in splinters of oak, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fully dislocated and there is no external wound, and only the joint is dislocated, not broken in two where the corbel sits inside, then it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the dislocation is on the right side, you should place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if it is on the left side, then use the index finger of your right hand, and push the joint gently back into place, and adjust it evenly with the other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the joint of the jaw is displaced to one side, you should administer an extension of one part, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth, or dislocation, then bind it with a thread of gold or silver or silk; then put a cerote on the jaw, and put a double drape over it; and place a large, well-shaped splint, or a piece of leather the same size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it in place as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then loosen it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and put plaster on top of it, made from powdered millstone with egg white or flour, after removing the cerate; and then apply another light plaster on top, and if the plasters adhere, and the condition of the malady does not change, leave it until it is healed; often it is healed in 3 weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone has been removed; then remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flames according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, then close the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to promote healing, until it is cured.
de la forcele	of the foreskin
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The foreskin can tear in many ways, toward the shoulder, and there are three types of tears: one where it is torn and separated into two pieces, which is the lightest injury to treat; another where there is a tear with a wound; and lastly, where the entire foreskin is torn off, which is the most serious injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure for when there is no wound with the tear is to have two attendants, one of whom holds the shoulder where the foreskin is torn, and the other stretches the neck toward the affected area; then, using your fingers, bring the torn edges together so that they are aligned, with no gaps or overlaps.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, then place under the shoulder of the patient a round pillow of cloth or wool, as thick as necessary; and hold it lightly in your hand, and press the pillow with your hand so that you make the break even as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out of joint because it is dislocated, then the patient should lie on his back, and place under the shoulder a small pillow, and the assistant should press the shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then stretch the break with your fingers, and if you find it broken, then you should split it open; and pull the pieces gently apart, and if the bone cannot join because of any swelling, then cut one of the incisions that you have made larger, but place this instrument under the shoulder to guard against the synovial sac:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and is shaped like a spoon, and is not hollow, and is as wide as it needs to be according to the size of the bone and the extent of the wound; and has .ij. edges, so that one is wide and the other narrow, just as the cut that you have made when you pulled the bones apart.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt the hot abscess, then pack the wound with bandages and dressings according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes out, moisten a bandage in rose oil and garlic and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The dislocation of the bone, when there is no wound or incision, is that you place on the bone an ointment made from mill-powder and egg white, and put light bandages on top, and if necessary, place a ball under the shoulder.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide band of one palm in width, then place a double bandage on the ointment, and then take a thin cloth six inches wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage is hanging loose.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the splint over the break, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy collarbone, and under the affected collarbone; and adjust it from each side, and when you see that the ligament is holding the break in place properly, and you clearly see that the splint is not moving on the broken bone, then release him each day, and when the ligature becomes loose, restrain him again.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps, put a small pillow under the collarbone to raise the shoulder; this will lighten the break in the clavicle by loosening the shoulder, or you can bind his arm to his neck, and do not untie it unless an evil accident happens, up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then resume the poultice if you see that he still needs it, and restrain him like this until he is healed; and it is usually healed within 28 days, but in some people less than that.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Then it happens that the shoulder breaks or widens in the middle, and one feels it only by touch; then prepare the apparatus according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way you can; then put flour from the mill with plenty of egg on the site, and light tampons, and place a double drape over it; then put a wide and thin board over it, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there is any swelling under the board on the shoulder, use that part of the swelling with linen tampons so that the board lies flat; and then tightly bind it with a large bandage so that the board does not move from its place, and check the ligature every day; and whenever it softens, bind it again, and adjust the board if it has moved, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored within 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is complete, loosen it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that sets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and not underneath the heart, pierce and open the bone, and do what we have said about the fracture of the collarbone to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downward, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a lack of strength, and swelling, and perhaps vomiting of blood, and the cracks in the broken bone become visible, and he feels great pain.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that the patient lies on his back, and places a cushion between his shoulders, then presses his shoulders together and brings his ribs closer together with his hands, carefully ensuring they are even on both sides, so that the bone is in the correct position; then he applies poultices and bandages made from fine salt or some other light material over the fracture, wrapping it in a cloth and securing it to the broken bone so it does not move; and he winds the ligature around the back again, tightening it gently, and checks every hour whether it has loosened, and if it has, he tightens it; and if it needs to be loosened because of corrosion or itching that has come over the area, or pain or an abscess, then he should do so promptly, removing the poultice and addressing the issue with appropriate treatments; then he reapplies the poultice and bandages, tightening them until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	about the breaking of ribs:
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You should know that rib fractures only occur in the thick part near the back, and in the front, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and it feels good when pressed on both sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put the break in place, as it should be. And then apply the ointment, and hold it in place with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.
